Westward Journey (7) 101

Such is Xianyang

Our inspection group to northern Shaanxi gathered in front of the Northwest Hotel at 9:30 AM on the 15th. We took cars to Sanyuan for inspection. As the cars started, dust billowed up again. Fortunately, the road was relatively flat at the beginning, so everyone didn't seem to mind. Soon, we reached the bank of the Wei River and saw the low, dilapidated walls of Xianyang city on the opposite bank. We couldn't help but sigh with regret. The Wei River was quite shallow and narrow, with the water flowing on the left side of the riverbed, only as wide as an ordinary stream. Where it was low and dry, there was no water, and the muddy soil was loose and difficult to walk on. Those crossing the river were first carried on the backs of camel drivers to the ferry. The reward they received was about ten to thirty copper coins per person each time. Once the ferry was full, it slowly started moving towards the opposite bank. The water flow in the Wei River was quite rapid, carrying a large amount of soil downstream. When it reached a flat area, the water flow slowed down slightly, and the sediment it carried settled at the bottom of the river. Continuing in this way, the riverbed became higher day by day, and the water flow was blocked and caused harm to the people. Although the buildings inside Xianyang city were not very crude, the scene was desolate. Looking back on the past, where is it now? In the city, besides the Wen Wang Temple and Zhang Yide Temple, there were no other ancient sites. Even the Afang Palace of Qin Shi Huang, where the emperors of the past competed in extravagance, was dozens of miles away from the city, with only a piece of yellow earth marking its ruins. The tombs of King Wen and King Wu of the Zhou Dynasty were located more than ten miles outside the city. There were more than ten stone tablets in front of each tomb, about as tall as a two-story Western-style building. Only a few sparse, withered green branches grew in front of them. The ground was bare, without any other plants. From here, the cars were difficult to drive due to the poor road conditions. After several tens of minutes, the road became wider again, but there were many bumps, and the shaking was so severe that it made people's heads spin. By the time we reached the Jing River at 2:30 PM, everyone's faces, eyes, and other parts of their bodies were covered by dust and dirt, almost turning into clay figures. The water flow in the Jing River seemed even more turbulent than that in the Wei River. Normally, the Jing River is clear and the Wei River is muddy, but on this day, the Jing River also carried a huge amount of yellow earth downstream. It could be said that the Jing and Wei rivers were indistinguishable. At 3:30 PM, the people and cars successively crossed to the other bank. We got back into the cars and continued towards Sanyuan. Along the way, we saw many jujube trees in one place, and a lot of cotton was also planted in the fields. Unfortunately, due to the lack of rainfall, it could not grow fully.

Around 5:30 PM, the cars arrived at Sanyuan. As we entered the city gate, representatives from various agencies were already waiting on the side of the road to greet us. Due to the temporary lack of suitable accommodation, we rested overnight in the county-run senior primary school. The school buildings were spacious. As soon as the team members arrived, they ordered servants to fetch water to wash away the dust, and the hospitality was very thoughtful. After 6:00 PM, the various political and business agencies of Sanyuan County hosted a banquet for us at the Mingde Pavilion Restaurant. At 9:00 PM, a welcoming party was held again at the school. On the morning of the 16th, County Magistrate Li and others planned to host another wash-the-dust banquet for us. We repeatedly declined, but to no avail, so we had to attend. However, Sanyuan has no mineral resources besides agricultural products. Therefore, in order to save time, Director Hu decided to depart at 8:00 AM that morning to Yao County, which is known for its coal, to conduct an inspection and perform statistical surveys.

We ultimately felt that statistical surveys were more practical and beneficial than empty, descriptive essays. For example, asking about the number of stamps sold by the local post office in a month can reveal the level of culture in that area. The same goes for other things. Therefore, as soon as we arrived at a slightly prosperous city, we asked shopkeepers about prices. As soon as we encountered farmers in the fields, we asked about the condition of agricultural products. If we encountered mining areas, many of the specialists brought machines and could perform tests as soon as they had the opportunity. In addition to oral inquiries, we could also obtain scientific proof. We believe that it is not very far from the word "inspection". Regarding Xianyang and Sanyuan, the results of our investigation during our short stay in the area are as follows:

(A) Xianyang (Population): There are about 1,000 households in Xianyang city, with a total of about 3,000 people. The entire county has about 79,000 people. (Area): About 3 million acres. (Land Tax): Divided into three types: military, civilian, and royal. [Military] Land is divided into three types. The tax collected per acre per year is about 40 to 50 cents. [Civilian] Land is divided into five grades. The tax collected per acre per year is about 10 to 50 cents. [Royal Land is not graded. About 40 to 50 cents per acre per year]. The annual tax revenue is about 110,000 yuan. (Cotton Production): The entire county produces about 3 million catties of cotton per year, with a tax of 8 li per catty. (Coal Price): Yaozhou coal is 2.6 yuan per 100 catties, and Shanxi coal is 3 yuan per 100 catties. (Other): Rapeseed oil is 1.3 yuan per catty, cotton oil is 1.34 yuan per catty, kerosene is 6.7 yuan per barrel, and the daily wage for labor is 30 cents, or about 40 yuan per year.

(B) Sanyuan (Population): The entire county has more than 11,000 households, with a total of about 90,000 people. (Area): 6,720 acres. (Land Tax): About 90,000 yuan. (Agriculture and Forestry): (1) Trees include mulberry, elm, willow, pine, poplar, cypress, soapberry, and tung. (2) Fruits include peaches, plums, apricots, persimmons, dates, pears, forest fruits, pomegranates, grapes, and papayas. (3) Grains include wheat, barley, buckwheat, broad beans, soybeans, mung beans, sword beans, sesame, millet, corn, taro, and sorghum. (4) Melons include watermelon, pumpkin, winter melon, gourd, squash, loofah, and angled gourd. (5) Vegetables include scallions, chives, garlic, eggplant, chili peppers, cabbage, lettuce, alfalfa, radish, and mustard. (6) Medicinal Herbs include Bupleurum, Cyperus rotundus, Artemisia, Agaricus, dried tangerine peel, Plantago, Sophora japonica, and sour jujube kernels. (Special Products): (1) Cotton: The entire county plants about 2,200 acres of cotton each year, with an average yield of 40 catties per acre, resulting in 8.92 million catties of cotton per year. (2) Linen Cloth: The spinning and weaving of linen cloth using traditional methods is mostly done by Shandong merchants. Because there is no fixed market, the annual output cannot be calculated. (Animals): Animals include cattle, horses, etc. Birds include chickens, ducks, etc. There are only two types of fish: carp and silver carp. (Transportation): (1) The post office is a second-class institution with one postmaster, one assistant, three letter carriers, and eight mail carriers. It serves five locations: Xi'an, Yao County, Tongzhou, Gaoling, and Chunhua. Mail is delivered daily between Xi'an and Gaoling, and every two to three days to the other locations. The daily revenue from postage is several hundred yuan. The remittance fees are extremely high, with 13 cents per yuan for remittances outside the province and 5 cents per hundred yuan within the province. (2) Cars: A car departs from Xi'an to Sanyuan once a day at 6:00 AM. The fare used to be 3.6 yuan per passenger, but now it has been reduced to 1.8 yuan due to competition. The route used to pass through Xianyang and was 130 li long, but now it takes a different route that is only 90 li long. Each truck can carry 600 catties of goods, with a charge of 3 yuan to Xi'an. (Education): The entire county has five complete primary schools, more than 160 elementary schools, 30 people's schools, four reading rooms, one sports field, one library, and one people's library. In addition, there is one provincial middle school and two county-run middle schools, but they have recently been suspended due to crop failures. The annual revenue includes: (1) A special tax of about 3,600 yuan per year, accounting for 40%. (2) Operating expenses from the Finance Bureau and the Education Department, about 7,000 yuan per year. (3) Tuition fees, 2,000 to 3,000 yuan per year. School property rental fees are about 2,000 yuan. Each school accommodates about 200 to 300 students. Each elementary school has only one or two classrooms, while complete primary schools have more than ten classrooms. Each grade has about 50 students. The oldest students in the highest grade are about 16 or 17 years old. Primary schools also have kindergartens. Tuition is waived for higher primary schools, while lower primary schools charge 2 yuan per year. Teachers' salaries are 10 to 12 yuan per month for lower primary schools and 12 to 20 yuan per month for higher primary schools. The principal receives about 24 yuan, with lodging provided but not meals. In addition, the Catholic Church also runs one primary school, and the Christian Church runs two primary schools, each with about 60 to 70 students, all tuition-free. Textbooks from the Commercial Press, China Book Company, and World Book Company are used. English is taught from the first grade of higher primary school (i.e., the fifth year of complete primary school). The teachers employed are all from Shaanxi, both male and female.

Since the above two counties are not within the inspection area, I have briefly recorded their general conditions as above. We will be departing for Yao County at 8:00 AM this morning. Since there are no cars, the difficulties will be even greater. As I write this, I hear the sound of rain dripping outside. It started at 2:00 AM, but stopped after less than half an hour. Farmers who have been longing for rain may not be satisfied with this small amount of rain. (Morning of the 16th)

A Jealous Murder Case in the Train Station Road Yesterday (23rd) at 8:52 AM, a passenger train from Shanghai arrived. Three female passengers, including Zhang Aibao, got off the train. While walking along the road, a man suddenly rushed out. The man, Hu Huayun from Yuhang, wielded an axe and a sharp knife, stabbing Zhang Aibao five times. When the man saw that he had caused trouble, he stabbed himself in the throat. However, the wound was shallow. A crowd quickly gathered and captured the assailant. A note written on the back of a cigarette pack was found on him, listing the names and addresses of the people he wanted to take revenge on. The reason for the attack was that Zhang Aibao had previously had a relationship with Hu Huayun. Zhang then changed to another lover, causing jealousy. It is reported that Hu is a carpenter. Knowing that Zhang would be arriving in Songjiang this morning, Hu came to Songjiang yesterday and stayed at the Mingli Inn. When the early train arrived in Songjiang, he was waiting on the road. The injured man and woman are currently being treated at Joseph's Hospital. The female passenger who accompanied them was taken back to the Public Security Bureau to be questioned and sent to the court for investigation.

Home
